FOREWORD

BY STEPHEN K. BANNON

An important and apocryphal story is often told about a secret meeting in Bejing in July 1971 between U.S. Secretary of State Henry Kissinger and Zhou Enlai, a leading figure in the Chinese Communist Party who served as a diplomat and the first Premier of the People’s Republic of China from 1954 until his death in 1976. He played a major role in the Chinese Revolution. As Kissinger recalled in his book, he asked Zhou Enlai what he thought about the success of the French Revolution. “Too soon to say,” Enlai replied.

While the veracity of that particular story has been challenged, the message is clear … human history is not a sprint. It is a marathon, its success is frequently challenged, and its endurance is not guaranteed.

In Unhumans, the authors focus on the critical matter of what actually makes us human. They note that “humanity” only happens when you have an actual civilization—principles of civility, rules of law and order, respect for basic human rights. Great civilizations have always organzied and risen from these characteristics, from the ancient world to the Roman Empire to the West today.

The authors argue that it is humanity itself currently under threat. They unwrap the history of Communism, a dehumanizing philosophy of oppression, of denial of human rights and nihilism. The reader is guided around the world, revealing the stories and histories the mainstream press won’t touch … from Cambodia, Nicaragua, Chile, Afghanistan and the Soviets, to Apartheid in South Africa. They bring us right up to President Donald Trump and January 6th, a day they correctly call “America’s Inverse Bastille.”

Jack Posobiec is a graduate of Temple University and a former Naval Intelligence Officer. He was deployed to Guantanamo Naval Base for ten months in 2012 and is fluent in Mandarin.

Joshua Lisec is a writer with over eighty books to his credit. Together, Jack and Joshua unwrap a dazzling yet dire history of Communism’s impact on humanity across the globe. From the Russian Revolution to the true story of the Spanish Civil War, they describe and explain the 1950s emergence of Cultural Marxism in the United States, and its current resurgence.

“Unhumans” simply refers to those Homo sapiens who seek nothing but destruction of human society, borne of grievance and misery and nihilism. Unquestionably, we are in a period of this unhuman ascension.

Unhumans is a clarion call to every American citizen. Be aware. Too often, the most dire and significant moments in history are only realized afterward, when civilizations are already defeated or too broken to continue.

If you love this country, read this book. Study this book. Share this book. And understand this: The very survival of the American Republic is now on the shoulders of every American.

c5P

INTRODUCTION

PETTY RESENTMENT AND CRUELTY

Communism is when ugly deformed freaks make it illegal to be normal then rob and/or kill all successful people out of petty resentment and cruelty. The ideology is all just window dressing.

—@MysteryGrove

This is not a book about communist ideology. You’ve read those. This is a book about the communist reality—and how to tell when it’s coming to a society near you.

History does not repeat, but it rhymes. For as long as there have been beauty and truth, love and life, there have also been the ugly liars who hate and kill. This is the way of things in all things. There is light and there is dark. Always has been. Always will be. Civilization is the superstructure built on law and order that keeps the petty, the resentful, and the cruel away from the rest of us. Some societies have been better at this than others. Those who fail at repelling the repulsive fall to unhumanity—to a state of affairs in which human thriving is impossible and surviving improbable.

It doesn’t matter what you call these the people of anti-civilization. They will change their name, shape, and form as needed and for their own purposes in their unique time and place. For the last couple centuries, we’ve known them as communists. Socialists, with extra steps. And of course, leftists. Radicals and revolutionaries as well. A hundred years ago, Marxist-Leninists, then more recently, Cultural Marxists. Even as, without irony and not as a joke, “progressives.” For the purposes of this book, we will call them the unhumans. This is a book about unhumans, and this is what they do: With power, unhumans undo civilization itself. They undo order. They undo the basic bonds of society that make communities and nations possible. They destroy the human rights of life, liberty, and property—and undo their own humanity in the process by fully embracing nihilism, cynicism, and envy.

“Unhuman”—isn’t that harsh? Yes, and it also happens to be correct. By becoming consumed by nihilism, unhumans oppose everything that makes up humanity. As they are opposed to humanity itself, they place themselves outside of the category completely, in an entirely new misery-driven subdivision, the unhuman. They specifically reject the human rights of others. So if and when they get their way, they will unhuman you, too. They convert, and that which they cannot convert, they destroy. And they will call this evil, good.

But that’s not how it starts. It all begins with a wedge between two identifiable groups in a given society—the haves, and the have-nots, which they prefer to call the oppressor and the oppressed, respectively. Now, many have-nots do aspire to more, and they earn every bit of it. But some of them stop dreaming. Some don’t in the first place. And the trouble is, these men and women find each other. They have shared grievances, real and imagined. And then … they unite. There are parades and protests. Then power. All of a sudden, it’s theirs, all theirs. Then they rob and they kill. Any ideology preached along the way is just window dressing.

They don’t believe what they say. They don’t care about winning debates. They don’t even want equality. They just want an excuse to destroy everything. They want an excuse to destroy you.

This is what they do.

And this book is how we stop them.

c6B

CHAPTER 1

SO YOU THINK YOU KNOW COMMUNISM

The first maxim of your policy ought to be to lead … the people’s enemies by terror.

—Maximilien Robespierre

Remember what it was like when you were a child. Did you ever have a bad dream? Most kids do. You might even remember what one of yours was about. When you’re little, most nightmares follow the same plot.

Everything starts out fine. Then all of a sudden, it’s not.

Something’s coming for you. It’s big. It’s scary.

And it sees you.

You run to hide.

But your legs feel stuck. It’s so slow, so hard to move.

It’s catching up.

You panic. Throat’s dry. Can’t stop.

You turn a corner. You’re in a hallway. You run. Keep running.

There’s a door.

But—it’s found you.

Huffing. Heaving. Snarling. Angry. Red eyes.

You open—no.

You can’t.

Door’s locked.

You pound.

No one hears. No one’s coming. Nowhere to run.

Here it comes.

You freeze.

…

And now you wake up.

Did that feel familiar? The most common nightmare we all have is being chased. It’s more than just a dream though. It’s one of the worst-case scenarios you could ever experience in real life. There’s impending doom, dread incarnate, and no way of escape. You run and run, separated and cornered, trapped. No wonder the panicked heartbeat wakes you up. It’s unsettling. Whether you have that bad dream at age five or fifty-five, you probably feel a little haunted for a few hours afterward.

For good reason. There was this predator. It felt so real. But it was worse than a hungry animal. Because it knew what it was doing. It saw you. It felt your fear. The more fear it felt, the bigger it got and the slower you ran. A little kid feels helpless in that dream. But the predator? Happy.

Evil thrives on one emotion above all others: terror.

And worst of all, they want you to feel that terror. Because by the time you do, it’s too late to do anything about it.

The first policy of the unhuman is terror, as Robespierre wrote to his fellow leftists.1 The proto-communist French Revolution left 30,000 dead by guillotine alone. But not before they all felt dread and saw their doom. The guillotine. Forced to walk up there, hands tied so tight wrists bleed. Hearing the cheers like a stadium. Surrounded by hate. No one coming to save them. They knew it. But they couldn’t wake up.

The communist uprising thrives on one emotion above all others. By the time you’re feeling it, it’s too late to do anything about it.

Wake up. Fight back.

If you don’t understand communist revolutions, you don’t understand the times in which we live. And if you do, then you understand it is time to take action. No one is coming to save us. It is up to us.

As we write this, law and order has been overturned. The prevailing order is in disarray. In fact, it is categorically disordered. In twenty-first-century America, accusations are now evidence; denial is guilt. Activism means open bigotry and actual hate—as long as it’s directed at certain unpopular people and “privileged” groups. All statements are taken out of context and twisted with dishonesty for a dunk. Nuance is the enemy. Normal is a problem, and problems are normalized. Crime is punished with neither bail nor jail. Voice concern and you face “lawfare”—financial death by a hundred bad-faith lawsuits. Speak louder and unleash a ravenous appetite for vengeance—to deplatform you, debank your family, and destroy your good name. No prospects for work, bank accounts closed or seized, and reputation in ruin. This is what they do.

To the unbiased observer, this is a cancerous set of tactics and obviously so. And yet they are no surprise. The news constantly documents all this insanity and hypocrisy, and none of it’s even new. Patterns of the past make sense of our present. And these patterns foretell a terrifying future we might be destined to endure. After all, “those who cannot remember the past are condemned to repeat it,” as the prescient George Santayana wrote in 1905.2

For nearly 250 years, far-left sociopolitical uprisings have followed the same battle plans—from first call for change, to the last innocent executed; from denial revolution is boiling over, to declaration of the new order.

Wait a minute, you’d be right to cut us off. Didn’t we all learn about communist history in school? Like Stalin, the Cold War, Jacobins, something about Angola … all that stuff?

You might think you know communism. You don’t.

Let us guess; you probably haven’t thought about CPUSA recently, have you? (That’s the Communist Party USA, FYI.) In fact, this might be the first time you’ve ever heard of them, or read of someone else mentioning them. Yes, CPUSA is a real political party, founded in 1919. No, they have no meaningful influence in modern America. So if that’s who you associate with “communism,” we encourage you to check your reds. The communist cause always has been and always will be a chameleon. Red has many shades. It complements whoever has the power to wedge a society into separate, angry factions, into isolated yet aligned groups of us versus them. At the time of this writing, CPUSA is the least of our worries. Communism has been rebranded, then and now. This is one of the many covert tactics of the red revolutionary this book reveals. And this conversion is the very reason that good, smart people are shocked, shocked, I say! when the revolution comes to their neighborhood. It’s in the word. Shocked. Everything starts out fine. Then all of a sudden, it’s not. Something’s after you.

Red terror. The victims never saw it coming. We wrote this book so you can. This is the untold story of how those who view the world through optics of groups that have power and groups that don’t bring down a culture, a country, and a civilization, all through communist revolution, by that very term or another.

This book is also the story of a playbook. A playbook that every far-left uprising, insurrection, and usurpation of order, goodwill, and freedom follows, in the precise order it follows, and what has been done to fight back, for good or for loss. Often, the unhumans do win; after all, the far left has a body count of 100 million. But they do not win every time. And not this time. Yes, the potential for red revolution is baked into every democratic society. Their success is not.

That said, this probably isn’t the first book on communism you’ve read. It might be the first you finish. Here’s why. While academic and reference titles explore the motives and agenda of household-name leaders during each left-wing upheaval, this book will give you on-the-ground descriptions of what it’s really like to witness (and fight) communist forces of change. We have recast the story of communism as individuals against individuals, as real people, to reveal how and why neighbors turn against neighbors. Why even yours might, against you. Along the way, we will reintroduce you to the household names of history, but in a way you’ve never seen before—we will tell their true stories.

And unlike some popular conservative commentators—who are nakedly reactionary and hyperbolically defeatist in their retellings of left-wing political history—this book will offer a measured tone. We will take this subject as seriously as deserved. And in the process, this book will inoculate you and by extension those you love from ever falling for revolutionary ideas that accelerate the end of everything. Throughout the book, we will suggest what to do about it. All of it. The unhumans have their playbook; now we’re giving you ours. You may skip to the counterrevolutionary system to win, detailed in Chapters 12 and 13, but we don’t think you’ll want to miss all the groundwork we lay before that. The biggest problem people have when dealing with politics is they think, What can I do though? I can’t make a difference. If this is what you think, allow us to prove you wrong.

We have a vested interest in this subject. We, your humble authors, Jack Posobiec and Joshua Lisec, are both fathers. Husbands. Businessmen. Investors in the future. We believe in beauty, truth, law, and order. We believe in the God-given will of the human spirit to build a greater, better world than the one we found ourselves in. And already, that one is gone; the civilization we were both born into no longer exists. There is only one force powerful enough to bring us to this point and beyond: the force of anti-civilization. Unhumanity. We oppose it to the end. There have been many such forces in history and prehistory alike. But those most effective at annihilating everything righteous people held dear—those who have been the “best” at robbing and killing—they have always been communists.

So join us on a sweeping and succinct journey through history to learn the untold stories of radical takeovers that textbooks, teachers, and TV documentaries don’t tell. From the plains of Spain to the jungles of southeast Asia, from the communist uprising that toppled America’s first ally and made a mockery of her righteous revolution, to the end of our own constitutional republic, we will reveal how a global death cult recruits new members, speaks different languages, and emerges on different continents—yet it has but one unchanging purpose: to unhuman anyone in its way. We will cover how this was done, by whom, and what was attempted (or ought to have been) to stop them in the times and places you think you know but may not, such as:

The French and Haitian Revolutions

The Russian Revolution and Civil War

The Spanish Civil War

The Chinese Civil War and Cultural Revolution

America’s 1960s Revolution and Culture War

… and more.

What lies ahead is the secret history of radical left-wing uprisings— the rebellions of the aggrieved. It is a warning from the past, to the present, about the unhumans. Theirs is a story more than two thousand years in the making, many episodes of which have gone unseen and unheard. This is the untold story of the communist revolution— and how to stop the next one.

We will explain that communism, like leftism, is not an ideology. It is a tactic of warfare. Communism is a tactic to take power wherever it is applied, and is solely focused on taking power. They launch microrevolutions against their targets. They use irregular warfare. They operate in the fifth-generation warfare grayzone in the modern world. We will explain.

To fight back, conservatives, centrists, moderates, and even good liberals will need to embrace something they have never considered. They must embrace exact reciprocity. That which is done by the communist and the regime must be done unto them. This includes embracing reciprocal lawfare. This includes embracing naming and shaming. This includes embracing boycotts. All of this and more.

The unhumans will not stop until they are stopped. And we must stop them.

c8J

CHAPTER 2

THE UNHUMANS ARE COMING

Those who can make you believe absurdities can make you commit atrocities.

—François Marie Arouet de Voltaire

Conservative authors and pundits have been writing about the left for forty-plus years. And for forty-plus years, the United States, and the West as a result, have moved to the Left. Why is this? Our thesis is that the conservative movement has failed to conserve anything worth conserving. This is why we are in the situation we currently find ourselves in, and it is in fact a state of learned helplessness.

Conservatives, centrists, and the right wing lose to the Left because they do not fundamentally understand the Left. Let this be a software upgrade to all who read this. The Cultural Marxist knows that the conservative will cry foul. The conservative will lash out with angry tweets about double standards and hypocrisy. But the Cultural Marxist does not care. The Cultural Marxist views everyone else as either unaware of the goal of the revolution, less than them, or an obstacle standing in their way to be destroyed. Only the revolution matters to the revolutionary. Conservatives have lost years of ground by being obsessed with debating “facts and logic” rather than doing the grubby work of entering institutions and remaking them from inside. The revolutionaries are a generation ahead in this regard. Conservatives are playing catch-up, and the hour is growing late. Time is short. Ultimately, the revolutionary does not care what the conservative says about them. They aren’t operating in good faith. These aren’t the unintentional consequences of good intentions. Conservatives need to wake up, and wake up now. This is a playbook that has been around longer than the United States itself. And we are reaching the endgame.

But how did we arrive here? Let’s go back to how a communist revolution begins. It begins with resentment. Resentment is an emotion bred by those who lose the lottery of life. It’s not fair, as life never is. But it should be fair, shouldn’t it? Those who got more, by luck or by work, should have less. That’s only fair. Isn’t it?

You’ve had these thoughts in your life. Everyone has. But you probably never thought that you should kill the people who have more than you. That you should destroy them and their families and all the things they built. Sure you’ve felt jealous from time to time, but you tamp it down. You’re a human, after all. You’d never act on it. And you certainly never formed a group of like-minded individuals to take those thoughts and put them into action. Such a thing would be criminal. It would be anti-civilizational in the highest order. It would be to deny humanity itself. It would be, in a word, unhuman.

Vladimir Lenin founded the Russian Communist Party in 1912 and the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics (USSR) not long after. He was among other things a master persuader. His open-air speeches and widely distributed writings oozed the politics of resentment. Lenin’s hatred for the aristocrats of Russia was palpable. He truly hated the Christian Russian imperials, lords of the many nationalities that the empire encompassed. And his speeches were, of course, persuasive. To whom? To those at the bottom of society: vagrants, thieves, violent criminals, various minorities, and the overall unsuccessful. Lenin would go on to build a new society right on top of the old one, with the bodies of Russian imperials as his bricks. Lenin added something to Marxism. Communist philosopher Karl Marx had thought the workers would eventually rise up on their own. Lenin decided things needed to be sped up through use of a revolutionary vanguard. This became the basis for Leninsim.

The Bolsheviks—these were his earliest followers. In Russian, the word means “the majority.” Indeed, many people then and there and here and now feel slighted by life at best, cheated and taken advantage of at worst. No one has ever said life is fair. It isn’t. That’s not how it works. There are always going to be winners and losers. It’s a simple fact of life. But when that fact gets turned into a movement born of anger and vengeance, the violence is never far away. The unhumans bring it.

Vladimir Lenin was chief unhuman of his day. Millions would die under his revolution and later his regime. This, to the Bolshevik mind, was good. Fair. From the haves, everything was taken: life, liberty, property. Envy and vengeance unleashed. A broken world was not repaired; it was, to use a favorite left-ism, “dismantled.” But that does not mean Russia’s have-nots got their justice or even equality. They did not. Lenin brought no great reforms to ease burdens or alleviate (or prevent) suffering. No, the communist Bolsheviks robbed and they killed. Everyone, everywhere, who would not pledge allegiance to the cause or stood in the way. Many who did were killed anyway. This is what they do.

Here is what conservatives still fail to grasp:

Unhumans still support communism after it killed 100 million people in the twentieth century. They are not bothered that communism killed 100 million people. In fact, they think 100 million deaths is just a good start. Those wholly possessed by resentment want to 10X that number. On a base level, unhumans seek the death of the successful and the desecration of the beautiful. They want to smash civilization. And so whenever and wherever they gain power, they do. And yet, conservatives would rather whine about equal treatment while unhumans are drawing them toward freshly dug graves.

Unhumans live to persecute the normal, once they take power. Anyone who calls them out for the crime of noticing their schemes is then subjected to a “struggle session.” They’re humiliated, unpersoned. In this way, victims of the far left become unhuman themselves, brought down to the resenters’ gutter. The purpose of a system is what it does. Radicals cow the middle into silence, for anyone could lose everything by speaking up. And so they do. It’s only fair, they say.

You’ll notice throughout this book the persistent, perennial unhuman obsession with clichéd sociopolitical objectives like “fairness” and “equality.” I am equal to you, the have-nots always say to the haves. But their meaning is not what the Founding Fathers spoke of with regard to equality under law. This, Friedrich Nietzsche understood. Nietzsche is quoted as saying, “No one is more inferior than those who insist on being equal.” The unhuman desires not to build a better world than the old one with its very real and also feigned issues, but to cut down and destroy all individual achievement and cultural greatness so that the world is as miserable as they are.

Wherever they emerge, unhumans first begin by amassing a following. Mass media programming is key for domination, for the mental conditioning that their way is the best way, the only way, the fair way. This is how relativistic multiculturalism was embedded into the Western psyche, by the way, this ubiquitous belief that no one culture or society is better than another so can’t we all just get along. And yet no country or people on earth lived in such a way naturally for all of history. When mass migration dilutes and unbalances a shared culture, there is one force alone powerful enough to hold it all together: an all-powerful state at the center. Only great empires have maintained multiple ethnic groups living within their borders simultaneously, keeping everyone in line with the overwhelming power of the emperor’s unyielding hand. These were not republics with civil liberties and equal standing for all classes. It is unlikely a republic could exist in such a condition. Be careful what you wish for, conservative.

The conservative fails to comprehend that freedom cannot exist in the sociopolitical sense without shared culture and shared value systems that agree on what freedom is and from what (or Whom) it derives. Without common culture, only that all-powerful government can keep diverse populations from ethnic, religious, and other conflicts—until they have had time to assimilate, that is. Consider how Irish, Italians, Germans, Polish, and other Euro-American groups fought against one another in nineteenth-century American cities. And yet today, all are simply “white Americans.” In Colonial America, the division was mostly along religious lines. Now, there is peace between and among them. Why? Common culture—American culture inherited from Western civilization. Neither a nation nor a city can be constituted from any chance collection of people, or in any chance period of time, without assimilation into a new metagroup to which all groups belong, e.g., “American” versus “Irish American,” “Italian American,” and so on. Indeed, most of history’s cities that admitted settlers, either at the time of their founding or later, have been troubled by warring factions, usually factions of people of have-not status. But to the unhuman, they see mass migration differently. This is not a problem, to the unhuman. It is an opportunity. “It is a mark of a tyrant to have men of foreign extraction rather than citizens as guests at table and companions, feeling that citizens are hostile but strangers make no claim against him,” wrote Aristotle.1

Notice the clear assignment of have and have-not roles in the context of unassimilated mass migration into preexisting cultures. Citizens are the oppressors; they have rights, responsibilities, and more. And those entering their territory, legally or illegally, are immediately the oppressed, for they have not those rights or responsibilities. They are stuck in the fringes of society, and do not have access to the wider economic and cultural life of the country. Even this group is further separated into who is oppressed the most. Legal immigrants are deemed more prosperous than illegal migrants and thus are subjected to cruel and unusual legal torture. Ask anyone who has attempted to seek legal immigration status much less citizenship in the United States and you will be left in disbelief if not tears; the US immigration system is currently a form of anarcho-tyranny. The purpose of a system is what it does. And the purpose of United States immigration law is to benefit the have-nots and the expense of all others. It’s unfair that not everyone can afford an immigration lawyer. And so those who can’t or won’t are thus granted special status—that of the oppressed.

Unhumans in command of a political apparatus, be that an immigration system, criminal justice, or otherwise, indulge in anarcho-tyranny. This explains much about immigration, among other issues plaguing empires and republics of past and present for reasons Aristotle elucidated.

What is this anarcho-tyranny? Anarcho-tyranny is the selective overenforcement of laws against a target population alongside the selected nonenforcement of laws on another target population. This is the case in the present-day United States, as it has been in all societies being groomed for radical takeover and violent revolution. Perhaps the most famous illustration of real-world anarcho-tyranny is one attributed to Aleksandr Solzhenitsyn, author of The Gulag Archipelago and chronicler of numerous Lenin and Joseph Stalin–era crimes against humanity:

For him to have a knife was mere misbehavior, tradition, he didn’t know any better. But for you to have one was “terrorism.”

It is the oppressed who are released on account of mere misbehavior, their prior tradition, or lack of knowledge. It’s only fair. And for the oppressors from here, well, you should have known better. You will be punished to the fullest extent. Will conservatives ever figure this out, or will they continue to impotently point out double standards? Only action and reciprocity will change the behavior of the revolutionary.

Unhumans then and now are known for criminalizing self-defense and defending criminals. Again from Solzhenitsyn:

In the Criminal Code of 1926, there was a most stupid Article 139—“on the limits of necessary self-defense”—according to which you had the right to unsheath your knife only after the criminal’s knife was hovering over you.

And you could stab him only after he had stabbed you. Otherwise, you would be the one put on trial. (And there was no article in our legislation saying that the greater criminal was the one who attacked someone weaker than himself.)

This fear of exceeding the measure of necessary self-defense led to total spinelessness as a national characteristic.

A hoodlum once began to beat up the Red Army man Aleksandr Zakharov outside a club.

Zakharov took out a folding penknife and killed the hoodlum. And for this, he got ten years for plain murder! “And what was I supposed to do?” he asked, astonished. Prosecutor Artsishevsky replied: “You should have fled!”2

Unhumans live in a dark alternate reality where “should” is an argument, suspending all critical thought. If you do not do as you “should” have, and as criminals do as they “should” not, only law-abiding citizens are going to have a bad time.

Past, meet present. We witnessed this inversion of law and order to a cartoonish extent in the summer of 2020. On May 25, 2020, in Minneapolis, Minnesota, eight-time convicted criminal George Floyd was stopped by police officers on suspicion of attempting to pass a counterfeit bill. What happened in the next few minutes drew more attention from the global public than the year’s COVID-19 pandemic.3 You probably know. Officer Derek Chauvin restrained a cuffed Floyd on the ground, who famously said, “I can’t breathe.” In fact, he said this before he was even placed on the ground. Floyd’s death was later ruled a homicide by the county chief medical examiner, and Chauvin was sentenced to twenty-two-and-a-half years in prison for murder. What was lost among the international ire and calls for Chauvin’s head were other facts of the matter, such as:

Floyd had both fentanyl and methamphetamine in his system at time of death.4 Specifically, he had 11 ng/mL of fentanyl in his system.5 “Blood concentrations of approximately 7 ng/ml or greater have been associated with fatalities where poly-substance use was involved.”6

“If he were found dead at home alone and no other apparent causes, this could be acceptable to call an OD,” wrote that same county medical examiner, seemingly telling a different story in private than public.7 “That is a fatal level of fentanyl under normal circumstances,” he wrote elsewhere.8

In March 2020, two months prior to the altercation with Minneapolis police, Floyd had overdosed so severely he was hospitalized.9

In April, Floyd had contracted COVID-19. In the autopsy, Floyd tested positive for coronavirus.10

The autopsy, freely available online, states these words: “No life-threatening injuries identified.”11

Floyd had underlying conditions including heart disease, with one artery blocked 75 percent.12, 13

Despite all this evidence, the only verdict that could have been issued was guilty. Why? The American mind had already adopted the oppressor versus oppressed frame. And in this context, the white Chauvin was the oppressor and the black Floyd oppressed. Therefore, any and all possible if not likely causes of Floyd’s death that were not the fault of police were dismissed, by the public, the jury, and local authorities. (One of the jurors condemning Chauvin apparently lied to the judge, claiming no prior knowledge of Floyd’s death despite having publicly posted about his anti-police activism and attending George Floyd rallies in the months after the news broke.14)

To sum the story up, in the oppressor-oppressed context, Floyd “didn’t know any better;” he couldn’t have possibly died from anything other than premeditated murder. Mindset has consequences.

Now, all this background is necessary to understand the context of the police-free zones in Seattle, Washington and Portland, Oregon. In the wake of Floyd’s death and Chauvin’s arrest, there were more than 7,750 demonstrations in protest, with upward of 26 million Americans participating across more than 40 percent of all counties in the US.15, 16, 17 Some protesters stuck around after the initial marches and riots. Such was the case in both Seattle and Portland, where up went tent cities and out went the police. Among other events, the declaration of the “Capitol Hill Autonomous Zone” or CHAZ, in Seattle, with a copycat soon after in Portland. Seattle’s CHAZ began like many protests and riots did that summer, as an organized national uprising by the so-called oppressed against their oppressors—specifically, the black community versus the police. Of course, in Seattle, most people on both sides were white. In Seattle, city police abandoned the East Precinct building following nightly swarms of protesters; police and staff there deemed the mobs a safety risk and withdrew for their own protection. Protesters got right to building a communist microutopia, with emergent leaders declaring the area’s independence from all recognized authority. It would be hilarious if it weren’t lawless— and soon deadly.

Seattle mayor Jenny Durkan approved every bit of it. She reframed the anarchy of CHAZ as an attempt to “de-escalate interactions” between protesters and police, as tensions had been high following the popularized, politicized death of Floyd.18 The voices of more than one thousand counterprotesters who called for Durkan’s resignation went unheard.19 With police presence entirely removed, the CHAZ saw exactly what you’d expect: all the fixings of a hippie festival but with widespread looting and violence committed against small business owners and residents in the Capitol Hill neighborhood. There were multiple mass shootings and several murders, none of which have been officially solved. No one was coming to save the residents; they were hostages in their own homes. Some who escaped were prohibited by police from returning in hopes of saving valuables or defending their property. Across the CHAZ, there was sexual assault (as there had been during the infamous Occupy Wall Street protests that inspired CHAZ) and also arson, all effectively city-sanctioned.20 Anarcho-tyranny. This is what they do. (All of this, including firsthand experiences in CHAZ, are further detailed in Posobiec’s book The Antifa: Stories from Inside the Black Bloc, published 2021.)

Consider what you might be feeling right now. Indignation. Righteous anger. Your mind begins to wander … to what you would do, in a CHAZ near you. When it’s illegal to defend your liberty and property but legal to seize and destroy it. The Seattle CHAZ lasted twenty-four days; the one in Portland, five hours. How Did We Get Here?

For conservatives to receive their software upgrade to understand what’s really going on in the world, they have to understand the oppressor-oppressed filter through which all news, entertainment, education, and even law and policy are forced through before they reach them. This will take time, but we hope that by the end of this book, it will be a new filter and mental model to understand the world.

By and large, classic liberals, conservatives, and even moderates do not understand what is going on in a societal system where the chief institutions of consensus-making are controlled by radicals and infiltrated by unhumans. During the peak racial panic of 2020, when asked to guess how many unarmed black men were killed by police each year, the average person on the street would respond with outrageous numbers that seemed to merit the violent anti-police protests swarming cities nationwide and leaving whole neighborhoods in ruin and burning rubble. This is not conjecture. Of progressive Americans actually surveyed, more than half thought that black deaths at the hands of police number more than 1,000 per year. Half of conservatives polled got the answer wrong, too.23 The correct number is thirteen—according to the most comprehensive records available, compiled by of all places the Washington Post.24 Add to this the fact that “instances of police use of force remain exceedingly rare and that rates of fatal officer-involved shootings … are generally lower in the past 10 years than in decades past.”25

We have the unhuman-occupied media to thank for this skewed belief about the nature of reality, the Washington Post one of the guiltiest parties. Even the accurate number—thirteen, which was the number recorded in 2019—may be misleadingly high. WaPo’s own database opens with dishonest framing of Michael Brown as “unarmed black man.”26 But according to the official Department of Justice report, Brown attacked a police officer—Darren Wilson—and attempted to take his gun and kill him. Brown, also much larger than Wilson, appeared to be drawing his own weapon. Darren Wilson acted in self-defense. And yet his example demonstrates that the unhumans leave out the context of what “unarmed black men” were doing to get themselves shot. We saw that same narrative-bending with George Floyd and Derek Chauvin. This is what they do.

A recent Manhattan Institute report found cause and effect between misleading overemphasis on those few fatal officer-involved shootings in the black community each year, and negative racial bias in public perception of police.27 Meanwhile, an empirical study from Harvard University found no statistical difference between police shootings of black and white suspects.28

People who accept this and other narratives are known as “normies,” who could also be called “NPR-Americans” as they believe the “official” sources. They’ve endured two to three generations of social conditioning through the education system, mass media, and Hollywood to distort how they make sense of the world so that fake becomes real and real becomes racist conspiracy theory.

This is what bestselling author and persuasion expert Scott Adams calls the “two movies on one screen” phenomenon.29 When people have their mental model provided to them from misleading input provided by institutions opposed to the flourishing of the American citizen, they form completely false impressions of the world all around them, causing them to interpret fact and information through that false lens. This is why, for example, when a public figure complains of systemic racism impeding the progress of black Americans and they are asked to provide an example, they present their perception. Opinion. How it feels. Unfair. We don’t even need an example as controversial as the death of George Floyd to see this. The completely false perception of how our world works maps onto other sociopolitical matters beyond police violence.

Another two movies, one screen example was the outrage over the Nick Sandmann video, in which a young teenager stood on the steps on the Lincoln Memorial, face-to-face with a Native American chanter. This video went viral online on the left and was said to be an example of white nationalist harassment. Here was a have and a have-not, oppressor versus oppressed. The Washington Post and numerous other media outlets picked it up. And yet the video depicts no racism, bigotry, or anything at all to it. The high school student simply stood still with an awkward smile and said nothing to the Native American man. Why then did the media report it as an obvious example of emboldened white nationalism under President Donald J. Trump? Why did everyone who outrage-shared it “see” racism in the clip despite no verbal cues to such or physical gestures? This is due to coding. If you have been “coded” (programmed) for years by Hollywood content, progressive education, and the mass media to perceive a white male in a Make America Great Again hat as a racist oppressor and any and all Native Americans as oppressed victims, then that is what you will see in any given situation despite a total and complete lack of evidence. As it turns out, it was actually the Native American chanter who was harassing Sandmann and his classmates, who were simply visiting the Lincoln Memorial on a trip to DC.

The key to understanding this is the power of persuasion. If the institutions that create our society’s mental model are infiltrated by radicals who hate those they deem oppressors, then public perception is decided in advance. Millions of people—including white Americans, conservative Republicans, and even President Trump supporters—watched a video and “saw” an unrepentant white nationalist oppressing a brave Native American victim. This was a big problem, and conservatives did not push back on the narrative for at least twenty-four hours when the story first broke.

CHAPTER 3

SUN TZU RED: HOW COMMUNISTS WIN BEFORE FIGHTING

To subdue the enemy without fighting is the acme of skill.

—Sun Tzu, The Art of War

Imagine you wanted to end current society as we know it and remake it in your own image and vision. But you don’t have the nuclear launch codes to threaten leaders to step down. No bioweapons or other advanced technology either. You’re just a dude with a vendetta. Suppose you didn’t want to hurt any one specific person. You want to take out them all. All the enemies who uphold current society, and stand in your way, and those who look, talk, and work like them. You are the us and they are the them. So you want to destroy the society “they” built and maintain for themselves at your expense. How would you do it? Well, you’d infiltrate, subvert, and overturn the existing order is what you would do. You would stage a revolution. To do it, you would follow the path laid by every red revolutionary—a path that begins with a strategic advantage the guardians of that society did not foresee. You would stack the odds in your favor so heavily that it would almost be as though you were winning without ever fighting. Oh, you’d still fight. You’d just be locking up the odds of victory before that battle even began.

There is a method to weaponize madness. And the irony is that there is a similar procedure developed and deployed by the most orderly and disciplined institution you can think of: the United States military. This procedure enables winning before fighting and it is called “Operational Preparation of the Environment,” or OPE. OPE is inherently tied to US military special forces. (Our man Jack may know a thing or two about this from his prior employer.)

OPE is primarily an enabling tactic that facilitates future … operations. It is an amalgam of lesser activities combined to minimize surprise and manage uncertainty by leveraging the capabilities and assets at the disposal of special operations forces to shape the environment. The “environment” that is being shaped, or “prepared,” includes both the physical environment and “human terrain.”1

Special forces OPE can involve shaping operations. Shaping operations are small actions and changes to the environment to create the conditions for victory in the larger battle before the opponent even knows one is coming. The academic description that comes to us by way of the Pentagon gives us a lot to work with. The short of the long is that OPE reduces surprise and risk by influencing the places and people where and upon whom future activities will occur. Official US military documents explain the how of OPE’s what like so:

[OPE activities seek] to acquire real-time target-specific information to facilitate potential target prosecution and preliminary engagement of the target to find, fix, track, monitor, or influence the objective prior to conduct of operations.2

This additional layer completes our understanding, specifically the key phrases “target-specific” and “influence the objective.” It’s intelligence-gathering meets military operation, all before “conduct of operations.” It’s asymmetric information—we know something they don’t—and a panopticon—we can see you, but you can’t see us. If you’re the target, that’s terrifying. And we know the thing about terror—by the time it overcomes you, it’s too late.

In other words, effective operational preparers know who to target, where they are, what they’re up to, with whom, and why—to all but guarantee success when they do finally move on that unsuspecting target. It’s the Sun Tzu strategy: Win before fight. You can probably recall two or three famous military victories that relied on OPE, from George Washington crossing the Delaware to D-Day 1944. The brief we cite in the first OPE definition details recent intelligence and military fusion operations. For one high-profile example, OPE is ultimately how SEAL Team Six found and stormed Osama bin Laden’s compound without alerting the warlord-terrorist to their presence.

It turns out, what works for a covert mission also works on the masses and likewise to shed blood. Not of a few ultra-guilty men, but to innocents, too, and by the thousands.

Here’s how leftists operationally prepare a society for chaos and carnage.

The Pre-Revolution

When we extrapolate our understanding of OPE onto the pre-revolution, we can both hindcast and forecast exactly how communist revolutionaries employ it. This is what they do.

Every revolution begins the same way: Radicals divide and conquer society. Envy and hatred are a communicable virus and secondary infection, and they spread among the most “immunocompromised.” That is, the unhumans divide cultures into categories, then infect perceived allies who have the greatest grievances over alleged unfairness, actual inequality, or both. Historically, that separation has been done by economic class, but more recently by race, and gender, and by both immutable and mutable (changeable) characteristics. After the dividing comes the conquering; we’ll talk more about the latter in Chapter 4. For now, we’ll talk division strategy, as that’s how the unhumans and the angry masses who follow them “find, fix, track, monitor, or influence the objective.”

The great irony of all their effort is that whenever communists have successfully seized power, they inevitably create a new society with greater and clearly indisputable unfairness and inequality. Because somebody has to manage the transition to utopia, right? That’s the vanguard. More on that later. And so the power promised to the aggrieved many accrues to the few who are cruelest. This is what they do. Every. Single. Time. Communism, Marxism, Leninism, Stalinism, Leftism—whatever we call it—is not ideological. It’s tactical. As author Devon Eriksen writes:

Marxism isn’t an ideology at all … it’s a tactic. It is simply the weaponized narrative of unilateral oppressor and oppressed, applied to whatever problem the storyteller has.3

This is what they do.

How Radicals Prepare Your Environment for Destruction

Since the objective of OPE is to minimize the preparers’ own surprise and manage the uncertainty (risks) of an uprising, our objective is to minimize our surprise and raise their risk. The more communists know about you and your society, the more effective they can divide it. In turn, the more you know about how they do this, the better you can defend yourself and everything you hold dear. The unhumans are coming, but we can be ready for them.

Dividing a Society, in Three Simple Steps

In one word each, revolutionaries prepare the way for revolution by:

The Separation Stage

The Messaging Stage

The Infiltration Stage

Naturally, this three-part operation involves collecting real-time information about a society and doing something with it. We have broken this down into Communist OPE. Let’s start with the first step.

Communist OPE, Stage 1: The Separation

The pre-revolution playbook begins with separating a society into distinct categories according to grievance. In every time and at every place, this great sorting is into the haves and the have-nots. The haves are de facto oppressors and the have-nots, the oppressed. These are “the two great hostile camps,” as The Communist Manifesto states.4

The Separation Stage processes assignment of blame and guilt. That is, the have-nots, well, have not, because the haves, have. And the reason must be due to oppression. Oppressors oppress the oppressed. To prepare for an uprising, communists further “acquire real-time target-specific information” as to which specific classes, professions, races, genders, ages, and so on are likeliest to align with their cause—to self-report some grievance, real or imagined—and which are likeliest to oppose it. This is how that’s gone.

In pre-revolutionary Russia, the Separation Stage was not difficult; in fact, it was already underway prior to the arrival of Vladimir Lenin and his gang of thugs. Deep social divisions are the mark of all aging empires. There was real disenfranchisement from landownership. The Russian serfdom system paralleled slavery in the United States in many ways. Peasant laborers, born serfs, were slaves by another name until 1861. That’s when that system officially transitioned into debt slavery; serfs were given land but had to reimburse the landowner for it, which plunged them into exorbitant debt worse than current student loan interest rates.

During that period, any resistance to imperial rule, even peaceful, was crushed. Those behind primitive revolts and systematic strikes across industrializing Russia were treated like war criminals. In countries all around the world, the Industrial Revolution was a catalyst for great change, great concentration of wealth, and even greater social turmoil. Even the briefest reading of what life was like for the have-nots in nineteenth- and early twentieth-century Russia shows a deep longing for reform of the living standards of the common man. There were compassionate voices, like famed novelist Leo Tolstoy, who, in The Kingdom of God Is Within You, published in 1894, advocated nonviolent, Christian resistance to the ironclad Tsarist ways. That and other Tolstoy writings later moved Mahatma Gandhi to lead a peaceful uncoupling of India from the British empire. That, too, could have gone the way of the communist. But the Indian independence movement did not. In Russia, however, there were radical instigators who would have it another way.

Communists generally identify and exploit preexisting fissures in a society by creating a vision of hope and empowerment, with the promise that the utopia will be achieved once the existing social order is overthrown and anyone in the way thrown in jail or murdered. This promise soon accrued Russian communists—called Bolsheviks—a following. (In contrast to Russia, other oppressor-versus-oppressed divisions have been fake because the people of other times and places have been better off. Then when radicals have come to power, they were worse oppressors, but armed with literacy, electricity, planes, trains, and automobiles.)

The Separation Stage identifies and isolates the best candidates for the have category and those of the have-not. This was straightforward for the Bolsheviks prior to the 1917 Russian Revolution. There was the bourgeoisie, and there was the proletariat—the aristocrats, owners, and landlords, set against the working class, respectively. Alongside the urban laborers were the rural peasantry. Natural allies in the struggle against the Tsar.

There were also the supporters of Nicholas II, the royal dynasty, and the Russian traditions—and of course, those who stood to gain from Russian industrialization. Many of these individuals, as we will see, formed the White Army. However, anyone opposed to imperialism, aristocracy, and big business could become natural allies of the revolution. The Bolsheviks knew this.

But even among the communists there was internal strife. Another faction within the Russian Social Democratic Labor Party besides the Bolsheviks was the Mensheviks. They believed in glacial-paced socialist change rather than the bloody Bolshevik avalanche. Despite being on the same team, this made the Mensheviks enemies of change. Lenin was direct about this.

Fifteen years prior to the assassination of Tsar Nicholas II and the shocking murder of his wife and children, Lenin published What Is to Be Done?, which concludes that “the opportunist rearguard will be replaced by the genuine vanguard of the most revolutionary class.”5 Already, Lenin had identified (and rejected) those familiar with the philosophy and literature of Marxism but who were unwilling to engage in what his pamphlet describes as “militant Marxism.” But ultimately, a nation and people in long overdue need of reform and rights were promised both but received neither.

The communist takeover of Spain and the subsequent civil war follow the same plot points, both in the operational preparation of the environment for radical change and in the eventual violence itself. Where the details change is the time, the place, and the people.

The big stuff carries over. For example, the legacy of all feudal societies frustrates their transformation into industrial nations. The medieval world was built to prevent social mobility. This was of obvious benefit to some; the haves could keep having, and the have-nots could never take it. But free markets—capitalism—have done more than any other economic system to raise the world’s tired, poor, and huddled masses out of feudal stagnation and into self-generated prosperity.6 And yet The Communist Manifesto criticizes individual success; self-empowerment is ironically a knock against the free market system, to the unhuman.

The bourgeoisie has stripped of its halo every occupation hitherto honored and looked up to with reverent awe. It has converted the physician, the lawyer, the priest, the poet, the man of science, into its paid wage laborers.7

God forbid that doctors, lawyers, and inventors arc their own careers in the direction of greatest compensation. And of course, communists slaughter the clergy together with the freethinking artists once they take power, so that point is moot. In fact, every communist uprising targets the Church first. You understand why we call this business of revolution a tactic, not a philosophy. Its hypocrisy, contradiction, and illogic are features, not bugs.

The unhumans found Spain ripe for harvest. For centuries there, like much of the Old World, the haves were: the aristocracy and landowning elites with their large estates and control of the nation’s agricultural resources, the Catholic Church with their perennial social influence, merchants, and with the coming of the Industrial Revolution, industrialists. Meanwhile, the have-nots were and had been for just as long the majority of the population—peasants who worked the land, the urban poor who toiled and soiled in factories, miners whose blood/sweat/tears enriched the industrialists, and other day laborers who generally had no control over their own material fate.

The Communist Manifesto message of siccing the have-nots on the haves had spread around the world by the turn of the century. Vladimir Lenin gave it a structure in 1919 when he created the Communist International (Comintern), an organization of communist parties whose stated purpose was to use the Russian treasury he had seized to promote world revolution and whose actual purpose was to grant the newly formed Soviet Union total globalist control of all communist movements on earth. It lasted from 1919 to 1943. (See Communist OPE, Stage 2: Messaging to learn how the unhumans gained the trust of Spain’s working poor.)

What communists do anywhere, they do everywhere. And so the Separation Stage came to Spain. In the decades leading up to their civil war, leftists recognized inter-institutional conflicts they could exploit. There were, by the early 1930s, the royals, self-interested political parties, the military class, the Catalonia and Basque independence movements (which remain a thing to this day), the landowners, the Church, and again, all the have-nots who made up the vast majority of all populations across all areas of Spain: urban, rural, coastal.

With the situation in hand, the unhumans would go on to do what unhumans do: They raped and they murdered. In 1936, the left-wing Popular Front government launched an anti-Catholic campaign of terror and murdered thousands of clergy alongside devout believers—martyrs for the faith. Why this first? The Separation Stage had uniquely scapegoated the Catholic Church. Of all the “have” groups available to target and carry out robbing and killing against, the Church was the stablest. They had power and influence, which they had held with stability and honor for centuries even as monarchs and dictators came and went. And so the radical socialist republic of Spain would disestablish the Church when the time came, looting and burning churches, murdering priests and nuns (after raping them on altars) with impunity, and constructing sacrilegious tributes to communism, assembled with stolen icons and other sacred artifacts. An iconic photo from that period shows Spanish socialists shooting a statue of Jesus Christ, execution-style. This is what they do.

The unhumans of Spain would also come for the landowners, literally “separating” them from ownership of their land. Nice farmland you have there. Would be a shame if someone nationalized it. This happened a lot.

In China, the early years of communist influence prior to revolution were protracted and saw multiple wars, reforms, uprisings, and unrest that brought the two-thousand-year Chinese empire to an end. This occurred in 1911 with the abdication of the last emperor, Puyi, of the Qing dynasty, which had ruled since 1644. Imperial China had faced a multitude of challenges that eroded its power and legitimacy, eventually leading to the downfall of the old ways. These included:

The Opium Wars with the British Empire—1839–1842 then 1856–1860—which resulted in humiliating defeats for China and loss of economic sovereignty. That is putting it lightly.

The Taiping Rebellion of 1850–1864, one of the deadliest conflicts in history—20 million lives lost. There are a lot of large death counts in this book. This is one of the largest, and it wasn’t even racked up by leftists. Chinese communism would of course be responsible for anywhere from 35 million up to 100-plus million dead (most likely 50 million) since 1949 alone.8

The Boxer Rebellion of 1899–1901, which reflected widespread discontent with foreign influence and the Qing Empire’s inability to protect national sovereignty.

We could publish a ten-volume series on just these events and their ultimate consequences made manifest in the communist revolution that turned China red (in more ways than one). That said, we promised not a history book but historical insights, so we encourage you to do your own research if you are so curious. The past can be a great library you lose yourself in; we encourage you instead to make a lens of it for the present and the future: What is likeliest to happen, based on patterns that have played themselves out previously? In China, Spain, Russia, and elsewhere the unhumans have wielded power, those patterns have consistently included these OPE stages. Thus, we study China—just enough to understand how our times might emulate theirs and in what ways.

Prior to, during, and following China’s internal rebellions, social unrest, and foreign wars, the little guy hurt the worst. In fact, even in China today, this is referred to as the Century of Humiliation. These have-nots were whom you’d probably expect for that period and place: farmers, manual laborers, unions, the military rank and file, radical intellectuals, students, bureaucrats. Yes, even the educated felt they didn’t have enough. During the decline and fall of their empire, they were probably right.

Their enemies were of course the Qing dynasty, (mis)managing it all until 1911, various warlords, foreign business interests, and, characteristically, Christian missionaries, who were considered outsiders who hailed from prosperous yet dangerous adversaries—a threat to their ancient way of life.

If you know your history, Lenin’s Comintern directed Dutch communist Henk Sneevliet to found a Chinese communist party, run by disgruntled, radical locals. The postimperial era brought a once-in-a-multi-millennia chance to replace one system with an entirely new one. The success of the Russian revolution offered a convenient template to follow. And so the Chinese Communist Party, the CCP, was founded in Shanghai in 1921 with thirteen inaugural members— among them, Mao Zedong.9

And yet the CCP soon realized they needed to go their own way if communism would find lasting influence in China’s future. In The Rise and Fall of Communism, Archie Brown writes that early Chinese communists realized their coalition of fed-up have-nots would not be the proletariat of Marxism-Leninism but the peasantry. “The strong do what they can and the weak suffer what they must,” wrote Thucydides in History of the Peloponnesian War. That famous quote from the Athenian historian perfectly describes the lot of the late-stage Qing dynasty peasant classes. Whether rural or urban, illiterate or industrialized, China’s workforce of that period suffered all the consequences of war and rebellion and yet received none of the upsides (conflicts are always cash cows, to the privileged few). Wasn’t it time for the peasantry to have a say in their own future? Wouldn’t that just be … fair?

That said, Soviet allies of the early CCP thought this delineation unwise. Mao, who would soon emerge as the figurehead of Chinese communism, was encouraged not to organize the peasantry as his target group, those ones chosen to usher in red change. The Comintern preferred educated influencers to instigate uprising. To organize the peasantry was a Marxist heresy from their standpoint, preferring to organize leaders from the urban proletariat. Marx himself once described French farmers as “a bag of potatoes.” In Mao’s case, he initially attempted to bring the potatoes to the fight.

And that was that. The early CCP drew the line—if you profited from ways past, you were oppressors; if you suffered during that two-millennia status quo, you were oppressed.

Communist OPE, Stage 2: The Message

Once revolutionaries have identified and begun tracking who among the masses is most susceptible, the mass persuasion begins. The radicals create and distribute messaging crafted to cultivate maximum discontentment. Think of this tactic as “brand awareness” of the revolution. It’s not yet a call to action in the advertising sense, i.e., “Buy now! Sign up here! Kill the landlords!” Rather, the Messaging Stage is to inform and enforce perception of and anger over the have-nots’ lot in life—while assigning all blame to the perpetrating group(s), the haves.

The Messaging Stage is successful when the groups targeted for manipulation accept the oppressed frame. You should have more. You don’t. It’s their fault. What are you going to do about it? That question is left unanswered with specificity going into the third stage. That’s by design. Let uncertainty fester. Let tensions escalate. Let envy build and resentment foment. Meanwhile, the unhumans begin their “long march through the institutions,” or at least through the organizations they need in order to take the great leap forward, from the dividing to the conquering. Sometimes, that’s more a short walk. Either way, that’s Infiltration, Stage Three. Here’s Step Two.

In pre-revolutionary Russia, the Bolsheviks under Lenin’s leadership systematically built resentment among the working classes toward their rulers, effectively using persuasion like a viral contagion passed person-to-person, inflicting reminders of class division to foment hatred. They used grievances to inculcate power structures based on anger. (Remember, communists look for grievances to exploit for their own ends, and that includes offenses both real and imagined.)

Initially, the Bolsheviks framed the political narrative as a class struggle that could only end once the working class refused to put up with any further subjugation. This from Leon Trotsky was the gist of pre-revolutionary anti-Tsarist propaganda:

Whatever the conditions may be the proletariat must clearly see its path and take it consciously. Above everything else it must be free from illusions. And the worst illusion in all its history from which the proletariat has up till now suffered has always been reliance upon others.10

In other words, set yourself free. This was a compelling pitch to the overworked underclasses of imperial Russia. So, too, for the military, as they had suffered a humiliating defeat in the first modern war—the Russo-Japanese War just after the turn of the century—and World War I seemed to serve no purpose for Russia beyond the glory of the Tsar and defense of his kingdom, an opportunity to rally all peoples of the empire into unified support of Nicholas II.

The Bolsheviks used all media available to them to spread their message of hope and change: newspapers, pamphlets, posters, cinema, and of course speeches and rallies. And they went where their audience was. That meant factories, military barracks, the urban squalor, and rural communities. You have not, they have; here’s what we’re going to do about it, was the consistent takeaway across all media and messages. Those paying attention couldn’t not know where this was all going.

To widen their support base, the Bolsheviks got intersectional. They pledged self-determination to the diverse ethnic and national groups within the Russian empire, tapping into nationalist movements and discontent with imperial policies.11, 12, 13, 14 And to win over women, the communists promised gender equality, challenging traditional roles and thus appealing to working women disillusioned with societal limitations (i.e., no civil rights equal to those of men), not those hallucinated in the twenty-first century by fourth-wave feminists.15, 16

This was when the socialists enacted International Women’s Day, celebrated on March 8, the beginning of the Russian Revolution. Lenin and company also engaged the next generation, establishing youth organizations that encouraged young people to eschew traditional values and question the authority of their elders, fostering a generational divide that further fractured societal cohesion.17, 18

Lenin knew how to win. He knew who he needed to win. His backers needed him to win. And he played to win. Eventually, he would try to help Spanish leftists win, too.

In 1921, four years into Bolshevik rule in Russia, El Partido Comunista de España was founded in Spain. The Spanish Communist Party. They had broken off from the Spanish Socialist Workers’ Party because, like the Mensheviks before them, they regarded violent revolution to be in poor taste. They would not join Lenin’s Comintern. But the radicals of the party were willing to carbon-copy Bolshevism, so they split off, founded the Partido, and joined the Comintern separately.19

During his military rule from 1923 to 1930, Miguel Primo de Rivera suppressed the Spanish Communist Party by arresting its leaders. This kept its membership small and denied them the opportunity for mass protests, so they moved their activities abroad to France and worked with communist organizations in other countries. In France, they published manifestos and organized protests when Primo de Rivera visited Paris in 1926.

Obviously, open Bolshevik-like sentiment was unwelcome in Spain during de Rivera’s rule. Radicals had to be covert if they were to continue any operation in Spain. And they did, with a little help from some friends. La Asociación de Amigos de la Unión Soviética was founded in the 1920s. Friends of the Soviet Union was a Comintern op. While its stated purpose was to develop interest in the Soviet Union, its real purpose was to develop relationships with locals worldwide so that various Friends correspondents could place the propaganda the national headquarters of the Friends in the Soviet Union sent them and answered questions so that Soviet sympathizers were always well-informed. Propaganda included posters, newspaper articles, journals, art, movies, plays, music, and even travel to Russia. They even set up pen pals and had requests for matchmaking between citizens of Spain and Russia. Also, the Friends in the Soviet Union had a radio station broadcasting to Western Europe by the 1930s.20 All this occurred beneath de Rivera’s snout. Soon it would not need to.

By 1930, Miguel Primo de Rivera’s popularity had dwindled to the point that the only honorable way out was resignation and exile—to, ironically, Paris, where he had forced his prior enemies the Spanish communists to seek refuge. Out of the chaos, the left-wing Second Spanish Republic emerged. The pendulum then swung the other way when conservatives took control of the national government following elections in 1933.

Prepping Spain for revolution in the Messaging Stage differed from that of Russia in both reach and publicity. Lenin and Trotsky gave open-air speeches at large rallies; communists in Spain had to hide one nation over or keep their work on the down-low at home. But the true believers kept the faith. Those who had an ear to hear communist propaganda heard and took it to heart.

Communists in China found eagerness and built trust with peasantry of course, but also with the next generation—including laborers, yes, but also the professional class. “The hand that rocks the cradle is the hand that rules the world,” wrote poet William Ross Wallace. Communists then and now understand this. In postimperial China, the OPE was more than mere media messaging; it involved active recruiting. In Finding Allies and Making Revolution, Tony Saitch writes that the Socialist Youth Corps operated semi-openly, and Marxist Study Societies existed legally—the former, a recruiting pool for the CCP, and the latter, a legal way to disseminate Soviet propaganda in the new China.21 These groups existed even prior to the founding of the party. Consider why.

At that time, the rural and urban youth of China alike had lived many lifetimes in their short one. Two thousand years had come and gone; it was the end of their history. The new government, under Sun Yat-sen and his Nationalist Party, advocated for three principles: nationalism (of course), democracy, and the livelihood of the people. Part and parcel with this came a struggle for the fate of the fallen empire’s soul: What is China to become now? Over time, the Nationalist Party, particularly under Chiang Kai-shek, made clear that the livelihood of the Chinese meant open hostility toward communism. Democracy could coexist with no competitor. Chiang made that clear with a massacre of Shanghai communists in 1927. The communists would retaliate, of course, escalating a period of pre-revolutionary violence led by Mao Zedong aimed to trigger more peasant revolts by in part targeting one of their bitterest enemies—landlords. More on that shortly.

Note the contrast between the political right and left in China at that time. Nationalists offered order, conservative values, and a deep respect for tradition. But the early CCP offered young people belonging, sensemaking, and what we’ll call “reading the room.” Those youth corps and study groups surrounded likely radicals with people just like them—youngsters who wanted more for themselves, their class, and their nation. They also, through Soviet-inspired propaganda quietly distributed in meetings, quickly came to see China as the next country where a proletariat would necessarily defeat the bourgeoisie; the peasantry must rise up and overtake the powers that be. With the empire gone, that meant the Nationalists were chief among the enemies of change. Civil war would be the only recourse.

Until then, the CCP would speak to the hopes, dreams, pains, and fears of the young workers and students. Communists offered the vision of a “New China” free from oppression, where land was redistributed, rights were protected, and the country was industrialized and modernized. Messaging focused on the future, with readings and speeches and later with posters and films that depicted happy families, productive factories, and bountiful harvests under communism. The CCP “got” these kids in ways Nationalist sentiment did not.

We see absolutely no parallels with any of this in the modern-day USA. None at all.

Communist OPE, Stage 3: The Infiltration

Notice that what the dividing communists do is their conquering. Well, it’s almost conquering. It is a pre-conquering. Communists cast a shadow over their target while its back is turned. Once they’re cornered, it’s (almost) too late to avoid fate.

If all unhumans had were “the people” on their side—that is, those groups they’ve been able to convince are oppressed by an oppressor class—they would not have a distinct advantage. They would, to borrow leftist language, be “punching up.” Terror as a tool demands no way of escape. The monster is coming and the door is locked. So for the punch up to have the necessary impact for revolution, the unhumans must also punch down. They must wield actual power. To acquire it, they must infiltrate.

You see, instigators of the revolution need both individuals and institutions bought into the cause prior to the uprising. Think “inside men” and choke points together with sympathetic elites who stand to gain power, prestige, and profit from the upturning of society—from the squeezing of the middle by two iron fists.

Remember, operational preparation of the environment “shapes” the “human terrain.” A leftist cliché is “power to the people.” What that actually means in practice is power to the people who want power. And shaping the human terrain is how they get it. This is what they do.

In Russia, the Bolsheviks strategically infiltrated key social and political institutions, laying the groundwork for their eventual success in the 1917 revolution. They began by infiltrating “soviets,” which were workers’ and soldiers’ councils (yes, that’s the origin of the word), advocating for policies like direct worker control over production and Russia’s immediate withdrawal from World War I. These positions, highlighting the immediate needs and desires of workers and soldiers, contrasted with the moderate stance of the Mensheviks.

The Bolsheviks’ aggressive organization and propaganda efforts paid off as they gained significant influence within those soviets, particularly in crucial urban centers like Petrograd and Moscow. The All-Russian Congress of Soviets became a key arena for their activities, where they eventually secured a majority. This allowed them to claim legitimacy as the representatives of the workers and soldiers, bolstering their position in the eyes of the public.

With control over the soviets, the Bolsheviks established parallel authority structures to systematically undermine imperial institutions. They challenged the Orthodox Church by capitalizing on anticlerical sentiments, which further eroded the foundation of the old regime.

Controlling the narrative was crucial, so the Bolsheviks took over newspapers and other means of mass communication, using these platforms to deepen divisions and spread their revolutionary message. Everyone knows their flagship publication, Pravda. This control of information was instrumental in shaping public opinion and rallying support for their cause.

All this strategic positioning within key institutions culminated in the not one but two communist uprisings of 1917. In late winter early that year, Nicholas II abdicated on behalf of himself and his son. Then in October, with significant influence within the Petrograd Soviet and control over critical military units, the Bolsheviks orchestrated a coup, overthrowing the new provisional government. They transferred power directly to the soviets and established a new government with Lenin in command.

OPE enabled this, all of this. And after seizing power, the Bolsheviks acted swiftly to consolidate their hold on the new order. They suppressed rival political factions, including the Mensheviks, shutting down their newspapers, arresting their leaders, and restricting soviet membership exclusively to Bolshevik supporters. These actions squashed any significant opposition, enabling the Bolsheviks to cement their control and begin transforming Russian society in their image and likeness. The Bolshevik rollup of power was so swift and complete because they had so well-prepared the environment for operation.

In Spain, the Infiltration Stage was well under way by the early 1930s, as the local communist party was formed more than a decade prior.

We pick up that story following the conservative, traditionalist electoral victory of 1933. Socialists and the have-not laborers for whom they advocated were big mad. So mad that mass strikes struck the nation. In October 1934, a miners’ strike in the region of Asturias gave way to an armed uprising against the government. There and elsewhere, workers’ councils were formed and socialist policies were enacted to create a sort of anarchy-meets-parallel-government. Unhumans do what they must under pressure. That pressure came from none other than Francisco Franco, military director of the Spanish army’s General Staff at the time.

The clash between revolutionaries establishing fake laws and (dis)order, and the forces tasked with maintaining the previous ones would spill into the following years. In 1936, those covert connections made between Spanish communists and the Soviet Union would emerge as essential; the Soviets had been able to influence Spain through “cultural exchanges,” more insidious because the Comintern managed to look so innocent while duping the Spanish people.22

In 1936, the socialist Popular Front achieved victory in elections that year, with Manuel Azaña the new prime minister. Then the emboldened leftists terrorized Catholics and landlords nationwide. When Franco stepped back up and said, in effect, Not on my watch, the Soviet Union met its match. Communist forces worldwide were mobilized to support Azaña and the varying shades of left in his coalition, from the mostly peaceful to the nunkillers. During the Spanish Civil War proper, the organizational and institutional forces of the Soviet Union and various communist parties worldwide aided and abetted their Spanish amigos.23 The environment had been prepared.

China witnessed a more protracted period of Infiltration. The Comintern had gotten the Chinese Communist Party up and running, and they also held strong sway in the short-lived republican government of Sun Yat-Sen. Following the establishment of diplomatic relations between new China and the Soviet Union, the Russo-Chinese Information Bureau, beginning in the late 1920s, brought quiet Soviet influence into otherwise legitimate institutions.
